**Capital XXIV.**
On the treatment of flesh torn in the nose.
When various pieces of flesh grow together in the nose and some cause is assembled that resembles the sting of a scorpion or a polyp's growth; this illness is called polyps because it resembles that fish. And its flesh is cancerous, inflamed, and dark in color; but if it is not flesh of lion, then it is not of dark color.
Therefore in that which is not a fraudulent flesh of lion nor cancerous, you should make the illness cease between your palms and expose it to the sun, and rub its nose, and pluck out those pieces of flesh there. And properly extract that from the parted flesh, and properly incise what you have comprehended of those with sharp and subtle spatula, from one part until you know that all the flesh is removed; for if there remains any cause by which amputation is possible, then remove it also with one of the subtle instruments easily, so that nothing remains. But if there is an ulcer with blood or occurs an abscess, then you should stay until it is necessary; for if they are malignant abscesses, then cut and cauterize there until all the blood has been extracted and all cavities have been cleaned.
And properly let it be dressed in the nose with proper incisions of wine and water or vinegar. But if the nose is opened and moisture proceeds from it to the palate, then you should know that it is healed.
But if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, then you should know that within there is flesh dead in the full pus of the bones of the nose to which amputation has not reached.
Therefore you should insert filiform in there where there is some thickness, and tie it with knots, and pause between each knot the quantity of the finger or less, and remove the illness and insert one extremity of the thread into the nose with the hook or with any other cause that is possible for it.
And after this has been done, that it draw its odor through the canals of the nose, and be exhaled over its palate, for often children at school have seen it done in such manner, and it is an easy thing for whoever wishes to do it.
And properly pause the two extremities of the thread, one extremity that emerges over the nose and the other that remains in the nose, and properly apply a suture of flesh with the knots that are on the thread, and do this until you know that the flesh is joined with the knots of the thread.
And properly extract the thread, and pause in the nose with the abstraction of blood once a day, and do this for three days or more until the corrosive ointment has corrupted all that is raw of the flesh.
And properly at the end of the treatment, pause in the nose a lead canula for several days until it is healed.
But if you desire a dry cure, use this one.
And this is the form of the instrument called capipurge-maker with which oils and medicines are distilled in the nose:

"Chapter XXX."
"On the extraction of teeth."
"You should first relieve the tooth of its pain with all haste and care in every extraction of it, for there is no cause why you should postpone the view of it when it is extracted, because it is a substance which becomes elevated at the time of its extraction."
"But when it is necessary to extract that tooth, you should firmly be certain what is the painful tooth, for often the pain deceives and goes from one tooth to another which is healthy, and you extract that one and yet the pain does not cease until the diseased and painful tooth is extracted, as we have seen by experience in operations of barbers."
"Therefore when you are certain what tooth is painful, and know it well, then you should scrape around the tooth with a spatula having some virtue in it until it has dissolved from the gum of all its parts, and then remove that with your fingers, or with fine forceps little by little until that is completely removed."

Chapter XXXII.
"Of the treatment of prominent teeth above the others."
When teeth protrude beyond their natural course due to deformity of shape, especially in women and particularly elderly women, it is necessary for you to consider: if one tooth is not close to another tooth and no rearrangement or splint can be made thereupon, then that tooth should be extracted. But if the tooth is attached to another tooth, then incise that tooth with this instrument of which this is the form; it resembles a pork trotter and should be made from Indian steel with an extremely sharp tip.
And let your incision be such that you cut through that tooth in three days due to the hardness of the tooth, and do not damage any other teeth.
And if it is an erupted tooth requiring reduction, then grind it down with an Indian steel file of which this is the form
And let it all be made of Indian steel and well sharpened; let it have many small pointed ends like a file with which the teeth are made into needles, with which the tooth is ground down little by little over many days with ease, so that no other tooth is damaged or injured. And finally grind it down at the end, and polish it with a soft pumice stone
And if it is a tooth whose edge is broken and irritates the tongue, then you should grind down that edge until its roughness is smoothed out and flattened so that the tongue does not rub against it and speech is not impaired.
Chapter XXXIII
Of restoring damaged teeth with gold or silver foil
When it happens that teeth are damaged by concussion and removal due to percussion or a fall, and the patient cannot chew properly despite your efforts with medications meant to promote healing, then know that those which have been strengthened with gold foil, not silver, remain strong for many days. Silver tends to tarnish and become brittle over time, whereas gold never changes.
And let the foil be of such thinness and fineness according to the amount that can fit between the teeth. The way to prepare it is to take the foil and fold it double over two healthy teeth, and then twist it in two places between the broken parts until the foil reaches the healthy part of the other tooth. And then carefully work the foil into the broken part where you started, and strengthen your hand with skill and ease so that it is not damaged.
And let your grasp be firm with which you hold the foil between the roots of the teeth so that it does not slip out.
And then cut off the excess ends of the foil with forceps or scissors, and tuck them away in each place with care, and fold them over and hide them between the healthy tooth and the broken one, so that they do not cause injury to the tongue. And then press it down tightly like this with a stone.
But if it comes loose or breaks off, strengthen it again or those with another piece of foil in the same manner at all times.

Chapter XXXIX
Of extracting blood attached to the throat
When a leech is attached to the throat and it cannot be removed with medicines as we have said in the chapter on treatment with medicines, then consider this: examine the patient's throat under sunlight, since you have prepared an instrument made of bone which we have recommended for you.
Then if you see the leech, remove it with a small hook or with gentle tweezers, carefully.
And if it is not possible for you to remove it with that, then take a concave cannula and insert it into the patient's throat, and place a hot iron pin inside the cavity of the cannula, and do this several times (until the leech is dead and removed from the throat), and abstain from giving the patient any water for the rest of the day.
And then take a vein full of water that has been heated and press it on the patient's mouth, and wash his mouth with it; and do not swallow any of this water, but keep it in your mouth for an hour or so until the leech becomes numb from the heat.
But if it is not removed with this method that we have recommended, then fumigate the patient with sulfur or with asafoetida using the instrument that we have recommended for fumigating the uvula.
Do this, so that it may fall off.
And here is another method of operation in fumigation: take an earthen pot in which there are burning coals and cover the pot with a lid in the middle of which there is a hole, and place the extremity of the instrument in that hole; then start fumigating from above; place the patient's mouth at the extremity of the cannula, and close his mouth so that the smoke does not escape until you know that the smoke has reached the leech, for it will fall off immediately.
And if it does not fall off, then repeat the fumigation many times, and do not let the patient drink or eat salty foods or anything else, and do not give him any water until this treatment has been completed.
And this is the shape of the instrument with which one treats a leech in the throat when it is seen; and it resembles forceps as you can see, except that there may be some curvature: which is inserted into the throat and its extremity resembles the beak of an ibis, which is wide and rough like a file, so that when it grasps something, it does not let go.
Chapter XL
In this chapter is the sum of the sermon on the treatment of boils and their incision.
Boils are many species, of many kinds, according to their appearance, as they are mentioned in this book for each one.
And they are diverse in their perforation and incision methods, of which there are two kinds: one for the specific type of boils; and for what is extracted from them by humectation.
And the second method is according to the parts of the body where they occur, for a boil on the head is treated differently from one on the buttocks, and a boil on fatty tissue is different from one at a joint, and each has its own treatment method.
And moreover, there are some boils that should not be perforated but rather await their maturity or completion.
Some boils should be removed when they are hard and not allowed to reach maturity or completion, such as those near joints, for when a boil is near a joint its substance extends until it can burst, and often the ligaments or nerves of that joint are corrupted, causing contraction of that limb; or it is near a main limb, and if you delay perforating it until it is matured it may harm the main limb; or it is near the buttocks, then perforate it even if it is not yet matured; do not perforate one that is hard and incompletely digested, but rather one that is near the buttocks, so that you do not cause prolapse of its contents and elongation into the inner parts of the buttocks, resulting in a fistula. But know this: the time for perforating a boil is when it is matured.
Know that a boil is matured when there is a decrease in pain and fever, and a reduction of redness and pulsation, and the head of the boil is sharp-pointed, and other signs.
And know that perforation should be made in the location where the boil is purest and where the purulent matter comes out from the opening of the boil.
Always perform perforation along the length of the flesh or skin if boils are located in the areas of the chest or belly, and in the location of ligaments, tendons, nerves, arteries, and in any other hidden locations where reflection is not possible; for those that are reflected upon, use perforation according to that limb.
But when the boil is in fatty tissue, it is better to let perforation happen after digestion is completed according to what has been said; for if you perforate it before that time, the flesh of its opening will be prolonged and much putrid matter will come out, and often the lips of it are hardened and the depth of it is increased.
But some boils are perforated across the width of the flesh or skin due to necessity, or according to what that limb requires.
And you should perform a small perforation for smaller boils and a large, wide one for larger ones or many sections depending on the variety of sizes of the boils.
And there are other boils in which the boil should be incised with curved forceps and cut when it has begun to appear, as happens with those that occur in mumps and buboes.
"Of those that are situated in section having three angles; and of these is one in which it is inscribed thus like the figure of a mirror leaf, like the blisters of angles."
Of those where round section and crescent moon section are administered, similar to these.
But that one which is not like its superficial blisters of lions, you should pierce it with superficial or flat piercing alone.
And when the blister is large and has already collected much pus, you should pierce it and not worry about extracting all the matter at that hour; having extracted some of it, apply a poultice to the blister again the next day, and then extract a larger portion, doing this many times according to degrees until it is completely healed.
And especially if the patient is of a weak constitution, or pregnant woman, or young child, or elderly in decay, for the animal spirit many times is resolved with the exit of the pus, and quickly death may occur, so operate wisely.
Therefore guard this chapter with great caution, and especially the piercing that you perform on these blisters, taking care to cleanse the wounds and consider whether the wound of the blister is small or a flat section; then you should administer the remedies of lye or old cotton. And if the blister is large and the fissures of the piercing are many, then you should pause for some time until they heal together.
And if in the blister a portion of the skin is severed or concave at its circumference, then you should fill it with old cotton or thread made from linen cloth without moisture, just as when dressing wounds from cuts or scratches; strengthen that on the third day; and then proceed to treat it and heal it with whatever ointments are necessary until it is healed.
But if bleeding occurs during your operation, then you should administer water and vinegar mixed with linen cloth, pressing it on the location of the bleeding several times.
But if the bleeding persists, then it is necessary to administer remedies and treatment and powders which are recommended in many places throughout this book and its divisions.
But if it is wintertime and the location of the blister is a place with many nerves, then you should wrap powders in warm wine and oil and press them on those locations.
And if it is summer and the locations are fleshy, then you should press powders soaked in water and oil or wine and oil, and all of this should be done frequently until the third day, as we have said. Then you should dress the blister and cleanse it and administer to its cure whatever is appropriate for it until it is healed.
And this is what is necessary regarding the knowledge of the cure of blisters in general, but according to the way of distinction, I have already said how each type of blister should be cured individually, by chapters specifically.
Chapter XL.

Chapter 1 of the abscess that occurs due to twisting of nerves
Just as an abscess can occur in an artery or vein, similarly an abscess can also occur in nerves when they are struck or due to excessive exertion.
And it most often occurs in the locations of the extensor muscles or the heel, or in any location where joints are strained.
And it is a serious abscess, resembling the color of other flesh, and it has its greatest disposition without fever. When it becomes very tense, there is a sensation of numbness, as if in a state of stupor.
And it is not an abscess that occurs on the chest, but rather outside of it, and it extends to all parts without reaching the front or back parts.
Therefore, those that occur at the joints should not be covered with iron, for this would cause severe contraction.
But one that is on the head or forehead can be opened with a scalpel. But if it is a small abscess, then you should press it with your fingers and incise it with scissors.
And if it is large, then you should suspend it with a hook, scrape it out, and remove it. Then adjust the flap with sutures, and dress it until it heals.
Chapter 2
Regarding the incision of an abscess that occurs in the belly
There are certain men who have seen in the bellies of those and other parts of their bodies, tumors that are called funguals due to their similarity with fungi. Their root is subtle but their head is large. Sometimes their lips are turned inward, and they are either small or greatly magnified.
And I have seen one, and in his belly there were two tumors resembling fungi, with no difference between them, being small and white.
And the lips of these tumors were inverted and split open, and moisture flowed from them continuously.
Therefore I incised those tumors and removed one weighing eighteen ounces and the other six ounces.
And the procedure for their incision is this: first consider whether the illness is moist, and if the color of the tumor is white, moist, and has a subtle root. Then incise it with a broad scalpel, and have cauteries ready in the fire at hand, for many times much blood flows out during the section, and if blood comes out, cauterize it.
But if the illness is pale and fearful, beware of incising with iron. Instead, take fresh lead wire and insert it into the tumor according to the manner we have described, and leave it for two days.
Then adjust at the constriction of the lead wire; continue to insert lead until the tumor is completely absorbed and falls off without being touched.
But if the tumor has a large root, then its incision can cause fear and trembling, especially one that is in the belly.
But it is possible to incise most of it and then cauterize it so that it does not return.
And dress it until the wound heals.
But beware that you do not presume to incise a tumor that is of dark color, has little sensation, and is guarded well, for it is cancerous.
And I remember this in connection with cancer.
Chapter 52
Regarding the treatment of an umbilical hernia
An umbilical hernia is caused by many things: either by fissures of the skin that is over the belly, or from the tissue or bowel protruding through other ruptures; or by blood flowing from a vein or artery, as has been mentioned before, or by constricted wind in it.
But if it is due to a fissure of the skin and protrusion of tissue, then the color of the abscess will be similar to that of the flesh, with little pain. It will appear in various places. But if it is due to a prolapse of the bowel, then its location will be as we have described above, with great variation in position. When you press on it with your fingers, it disappears but soon returns. There is much noise and pain with it, and it becomes greatly enlarged during bathing or vigorous activity.
But if it is due to moisture, then there will be little noise and it will not disappear when you press on it with your hand. It will neither be constricted nor enlarged.
"When it's due to blood, then this abscess appears blackening."
"If it's due to flesh, then the abscess is severe, large and hard, and its amount varies."
"But if it's due to wind, then touching it feels like a lion."
"And the operation is to consider now if the prominence of the navel is due to arterial blood or veinous blood or wind, then you should be prohibited from treating it, because in this case there is fear and dread as I have taught you in the chapter where I spoke about apostemes by artery and vein."
"And if the prominence of the navel is due to the bowel or tissue, then you should command the patient to lie on their back and stay stretched out. Then, mark around the entire navel with your finger and then command them to turn onto their hands and knees but still over their two hands, and then surround the navel's area marked with a broad spatula. Then extend the mass of the abscess upwards using a large hot poultice, and finally bind it around firmly with a bandage or cloth in the appropriate manner."
"And then heat the middle of the extended abscess over the bowel and insert your finger into that spot to seek out the bowel. And if you find it and hold it with your fingers, then gently extract it and push it back inside the abdomen."
"And if you have found the tissue, then take a pair of forceps and cut out its excess."
"But if it is against your artery or vein, then surround that area and return to your operation. Then take two needles and insert them into those two strong threads and insert the two needles into the circuit you have made around the abscess in a cross-shaped manner, making sure they penetrate. And then stretch the abscess in four directions over the needles."
"And if you wish, remove the needles and allow the location to close up naturally with the stretched skin falling back into place. Or cut it open when it has softened and become supple, and then dress it using whatever is appropriate for wounds until it heals."
"And if the prominence of the navel is due to fat or humidity, then you should incise the abscess as we have said and extract the blood or humidity that you find in it. Then dress it with whatever is appropriate and ensure that the location is consolidated."

Chapter LX
Of the Extraction of a Bladder Stone

Chapter LXV
**On the Treatment of Intestinal Hernia.**
"Hernias occur due to a rupture that happens in the ciphac [ possibly referring to the diaphragm], stretched out over the abdomen on the side of the navel, causing some intestines to protrude through that opening."
"This rupture occurs either in the diaphragm or as a result of an incision made there. It can happen due to various causes such as percussion (blow), sneezing, coughing, heavy lifting, or severe exertion."
"And when it's due to an extension of the diaphragm, it happens gradually over time and not suddenly. It also tends to form an abscess between the chest and the abdomen because the diaphragm presses on the intestines."
"And when it's due to a rupture of the diaphragm, sharp sudden pain occurs initially. An abscess forms on either side of the spine near the chest wall, caused by the contents of the intestines herniating through the hole in the diaphragm."
"Sometimes, a portion of the intestine gets stuck outside the abdominal wall, and this type of hernia is called an 'incarcerated' or 'strangulated' hernia."
"Sometimes it causes bloating and discomfort, sometimes the intestines slip back into the abdomen through the opening in the diaphragm, where they can become trapped, causing significant pain, especially when pressed."
"And in the treatment of these conditions with iron, care must be taken to avoid damaging or cauterizing the tissues there."
"The manner of operating on this condition is as follows: first, the patient should be made to reduce their abdomen by pressing inward with both hands at the sides of their convexity. Then, place your hand on their chest and elevate their arms upwards."
"Then, grasp the spermatic cord where it passes over the pubis, and incise it throughout its length. Then, use forceps to hold open the two lips of the incision as needed."
"And if the incision is made long enough, then that portion of the hernia can be pushed back through it."
"Then, carefully excise any sac surrounding the herniated portions of the intestines until the white, glistening peritoneum of each side is exposed."
"Then, insert your finger between the white peritoneum and the hernial sac which is behind the testicle, carefully separating them from each other."
"Then, grasp the spermatic cord at its external portion with your left hand, and extend the white peritoneum upwards with your right hand, elevating the hernia along with it through the incision. Then, command the assistant to extend the hernia further upwards, while you dissolve any adhesions present behind using saline solution."
"And then check with your fingers that there is no bowel wrapped around in the white peritoneum." "But if you find any cause, then immediately reduce it back into the abdomen."
"Then, make an incision below the spermatic cord to allow for the free flow of blood and pus, as we have previously recommended."
"Then, apply lanolin soaked in oil to the wound and dress it; also apply the ligature that we have recommended (and occasionally cauterize the white peritoneum around the incision to prevent bleeding, as often happens). Then, leave the ligature in place to fall on its own."
"But if there is excessive bleeding, then hot water should be poured onto it and pressure applied until the bleeding stops as we have said."
"And then treat the wound with the usual care for wounds until it heals."
"Chapter 66."
"Of Ventous Hernia."
"In this hernia, there does not appear to be one that has been burned during its treatment with iron."
"And the first [servant] said that it was done as we had recommended in the hernia which is with pus: that you lie the vessels close to the section over that with facility of it; and close in the middle place around the aposteme with water that works that, until the vessels fall."
"And cure the wound as we have said until it is healed."
"Chapter 67."
"Of the dissection that is done in hernias."
"Sometimes there happens rupture in hernias as we have said, and it becomes inflamed."
"And they do not give the cause of the bowels to the physician; and if they do give [it], that is little; and it returns again in all hours."
"But if the time is prolonged with that, there is made an adjusted fissure in the scrotum until the bowel goes into the scrotum; and this happens because of the extension of the scrotum which is in the hernia as we have said, which causes the scrotum to be stretched out, and around it becomes softened and the place becomes apostematized and inflamed."
"And the cure of that is with cauterization as has been preceded by its narration."
"And sometimes it is cured with iron according to this manner: and that is that the patient lies on his back between two tables, and around the place of rupture of inflamed apostemes, it is dried by section across according to three fingers."
"And then strengthen the scrotum white which is under the cord until it becomes visible."
"And then take a rake and press that upon the prominent place of the scrotum, and press that on the front of the abdomen."
"And then cut the two prominent places over the extremity of the scrotum's rake, and join them together with a suture one to the other."
"And then extract the extremity of the rake, and do not put back the scrotum entirely, nor extend the wound, nor any other cause as you wish to know in the cure of intestinal hernia."
"And then cure that with the cure of wounds, and when you incise the skin, clean it and restore the wound until it is consolidated; for the scrotum is contracted and the prominence of rupture is not adjusted."
"And cauterization is better in this place, for it is closer to health."
"Chapter 68."
"Regarding the softening of the spermatic cord."
Frequently in some men, the spermatic cord becomes softened because the flesh that is between it becomes softened, and this can be felt through touch.
Therefore, it is necessary for the person treating him to make the patient lie on his back and cut away all the softened spermatic cord that is over the natural one; and then approximate both lips with a suture.
And if you wish, at the beginning, remove the excess softened spermatic cord with three or four stitches and close it tightly with a suture.
Then, cut between the sutures; and then treat for other wounds until it is healed and the stitches fall out.
"Chapter 69."
"Regarding castration."
Know that castration is forbidden by our law, but it is necessary to mention this in this book for two reasons: the first being that it falls within the knowledge of the physician when he is consulted about it, so that he may know how to treat him who suffers from it; and the second reason is that often we have had need of castration of other beasts for our own benefit because of those animals, such as horses, goats, pigs, and similar beasts.
And therefore I say that castration is performed in two ways: either by crushing or by cutting through the division [of the spermatic cord].
But in that which is done by crushing, the procedure is as follows: make the beast lie down on its back with its hindquarters immersed in water until the genitals are softened and limp and hanging down. And then take them with your hand so that they may be resolved and not appear detached from their touching [i.e., without pulling too hard].
But in castration performed by cutting and dividing, you should hold the beast down and press the spermatic cord of its testes with your left hand.
And then ligate the suspensiony ligament, and cut above each one with a single section so that two pieces result.
And then cut off those which you have castrated. Do not leave any cause on those of the scrotum, but remove the delicate scrotum which is over the testicles.
And this manner of castration is better done by crushing because crushing leaves no cause of the testes so that the beast desires copulation.
And then dress the wound so that it may heal properly.
Chapter LXX
On the treatment of hermaphroditism
Hermaphroditism in men occurs in two ways: one is when something appears that fills the space of the spermatic cord between two testes, resembling a vulva in form in which there are no testes.
And sometimes from it urine flows which is in the spermatic cord of the testes.
But in women there is only one kind: it is that the vulva above the pubis appears like two testes of a man, somewhat diminished at its opening just as in men's pudenda and two testes.
And the treatment is of three kinds for men and one kind for women. And it is necessary that you cut away those adhered tissues so that the emission of fluid from that may cease, and then dress them with treatment for other wounds.
And in the second kind of men's hermaphroditism where urine flows from what is in the spermatic cord of the testes, there is neither treatment nor operation for it.
Chapter XXI
On lentigo and flesh raised by causes of women
A true lentigo is firmly attached to natural causes which are roughened and appears flat with regular growth, but sometimes it is enlarged in some women to the point that it becomes spread out like that in men and may interfere with copulation.
Therefore you should grasp the excess of lentigo with your hand or with a poultice and cut it off.
But do not finish cutting too deeply, especially in front of the anus, lest bleeding occur.
And then dress it with treatment for wounds so that it may heal properly.
But flesh raised is flesh that grows in the pubic region until it fills up there, and truly resembles a tail (and for this reason some first called it "tail disease"); therefore we should cut it away just as we cut off lentigo, and dress it so that it may heal properly.
Chapter LXXII
On the treatment of hemorrhoids
Hemorrhoids are when the vulva is not perforated or has a small opening. And it may be either natural or accidental.
Accidental hemorrhoids occur due to a preceding illness and are caused by either adherent flesh, delicate scrotum, or thick skin.
And they occur either in front of the pubis or on the sides of it, or above it, or below it. They prohibit copulation and conception and childbirth, and truly prohibit menstruation.
The diagnosis of hemorrhoids is made by examining the vulva: if prolapse is apparent, it should be reduced; but if not apparent, you should search for them with your fingers or with a speculum.
But if prolapse is due to delicate scrotum and it has prolapsed between the two labia majora, then cut away that scrotum.
And if it is suspended between the two labia minora, then suspend your fingers from both sides of its edges.
And let the woman lie on her back with her buttocks raised, and then spread apart the two labia majora with force so that delicate scrotum may break open and prolapse be reduced.
And then take wool soaked in oil and place it on that area, and cover it with a bandage for one day so that the wound may not be consolidated.
But if the scrotum is thick and tough, then cut it away with a broad spatula or with myrtle leaves.
But if prolapse occurs due to flesh, then suspend that with a poultice and cut it away.
And use the medicines which stop bleeding without bites, such as aloe, dragon's blood, and frankincense mixed with egg white.
And then insert a wide lead cannula so that the wound may not heal too lightly.
Hold it for several days and apply hot water compresses.
And then dress it with other wound-healing treatments until healed.
Sometimes it happens that other flesh is born from the natural vulva, and then cut it away in this manner. But if this occurs due to a hard abscess in the vulva, then do not cut the hard abscess with any iron instrument.
Chapter LXXIII
"Treatment of hemorrhoids, tail, and red buttocks that occur in the cunt of women."
"Hemorrhoids are caused by the inflammation of many veins around that area, which constantly bleed; and when these hemorrhoids are old and hardened, they become piles."
"And as you have said in the division of species and their signs, I will say which of these receive treatment and which do not."
"Therefore, I say that hemorrhoids and piles when they are in the front of the anus and not apparent to the touch, at that time there is no need for cure with iron."
"But those which are in the opening of the anus and can be felt, are those which require treatment."
"And you must put the woman in a warm bath and then extend her buttocks with forceps or rough cloth, and incise those with razors."
"And then powder should be sprinkled over them where the blood flows from one of the incisive powders without biting, such as acacia and similar things."
"And then she should lie on her stomach for an hour, and then pause that in warm water."
"And if the bleeding of blood persists, then let her be seared in a decoction of sumach and of cork oak acorns and of millet grains and of similar things."
"And then take barley flour and mix it with honey and vinegar, and make a plaster with that over her back."
"And if the blood is cut off, then it is good; but if not, then let it adhere with two leeches and let the nipples be scarified without cutting."
"And then take wool and immerse it in juice of cilantro or juice of hyssop or juice of rue with repent wine, and let it adhere to the place, and also cure the place with lint until it is healed."
"And cure it until it is healed."
"Chapter seventy-four."
"Of accidental perforation of the bladder."
"Many kinds of tumors accidentally occurring in the bladder, such as cancer and tumors that ulcerate and adhere and infiltrate and fester and form fistulas that bleed and secrete pus and bile and other tumors." "And then you should make the woman lie on her back with two pillows under her head; she should recline on her shoulders and adjust her weight to where the tumor is pushing out below the belly, and let her knees be spread apart, and pause her hands away from her thighs, and tie each one with a bandage convenient for water."

"But if the instrument is larger than the opening of the bladder, then it is necessary that you should place poultices on the tissues around the opening of the bladder so that the entry of any instrument into the opening of the bladder is prohibited."
"And it is necessary that you should place the point that runs in the instrument on the right side and above, and that the person who administers it holds the instrument and turns the point until the opening of the bladder is opened."
"And when the outlet appears, and it is touched with the hand and it is hot and moist, then it is necessary that you should dry it with a wide spatula."
"And when the urine is evacuated, then it is necessary that you should place in the wound a gauze soaked in rose oil or green oil in which there is some astringent; and press the catheter on the section in the opening of the bladder."
"And then cover the bladder with clean cotton wool soaked in water in which mallows have been boiled."
"And let it be cared for properly for two days, anointing it with that ointment convenient for this until it is healed."
"And sometimes the bladder and the wound are washed with rose water and honey, and also with water in which either red roses or long-stemmed lilies have been boiled; and then it returns to being anointed."
"And if the wound is inside the bladder and it has been wounded, then it is necessary that you should prohibit its cure with iron; having care of it with what we have said in this division."
"Chapter LXXV."
"Chapter LXXV To teach midwives how to treat women who give birth according to an unnatural figure."
"Natural childbirth is necessary for the midwife to recognize at the start through signs of it. When you see a woman pressing her thighs apart and wishing to smell the air, and she is comforted by what is upon her during labor, and she hastens the exit of the infant, then you know that this birth follows the natural figure, and the second one hangs with its mouth or suspended or pendent from the navel."
"Therefore, when you see those signs, it is necessary that the belly of it [the infant] be compressed so that the embryo descends gently, and when it has descended upon its head, then let the second one come out, and may it be cleansed of those superfluities with good cleansing."
"But that which is another than this birth is unnatural and blameworthy; for when the embryo has exited upon its feet and the body of it has come out before the head of it and its feet, and one hand of it, or one foot of it, or the head of it and one hand of it, has come out, and then the rest of it is turned over onto its neck, this resembles those figures that are blameworthy."
"Therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in all of these causes, and that she guard against error and deception."
"And I have shown you the entire figure of those [birth positions], and what kind is in them so that it may be understood by this and it was placed upon this."
"When the head has exited upon its head by natural effort and it is vehement against the woman, and this birth is difficult for her and her strength has already been depleted, then let them make that plaster or whatever women have, and evaporate with hot water mixed with fenugreek seed and humid oil."
"And then let the midwife insert her hand between its buttocks, which are small and divided, and remove with that the second one or cut it with her nail within what is in her of humidity." "Then press upon the woman's belly until the child descends."

"Then command her to be pressed, or anointed, and make her sneeze with incense; and hold her mouth and nostrils closed for one hour, because the child will soon be forgotten."
"And if both of the child's shoulders have been forgotten at the beginning, then it is necessary for you to bring them out little by little with gentleness." "But if it does not obey the insertion, then place the woman on a cushion and lift her feet up, and then strike the cushion upon the ground; and let the woman be held so that she does not fall due to the shock."
"And if the shoulders are not easily turned and the child is dead, then cut them and extract the remainder of the child or tie the cord to its hand with cloth and extract it gently, because that one will be forgotten."
"When the child emerges upon its feet, then it is necessary for you to push those down and turn the child gently, and also scrape that with your nail, and also take one of its feet and extend it little by little."
"But when it is within the thighs, then command it to be pressed and make it sneeze with incense, because it will soon be forgotten if God wills."
"And if it is not forgotten with what we have described, then return the child little by little until you place it according to its natural figure, because it will soon be forgotten with gentle emergence."
"And if it is prohibited with everything that we have described, then take mastic powder and dissolved gum, grind them together well in the mortar, and then line with that the woman's mouth and the lower part of her belly." "And then make her drink hot water until she sweats from the hypochondria."
"And when sometimes the parts of childbirth are inflamed, then make her inhale steam from myrtle and apply poultices to her." "And when she has inhaled steam for one hour, then make her sit upon a cushion, and also make her sneeze and clear her mouth, and lift her up, and press the lower part of her belly gently, because the child will soon be forgotten."
"Emergence of the child laterally while one of its shoulders is pendant." "It should be gently reduced by the hand of the midwife, but if you cannot reduce it, then raise the woman and make her walk."
"And if she cannot walk, then have her lie upon the bed and strike its buttocks with violent blows, and also administer remedies which you know and have described of mucilages."
"And if the childbirth has come, then make her sit upon a cushion, and study upon the reduction by hand, and scrape the child according to its natural figure, and make the woman sneeze and command her to press herself until it is forgotten."
"Emergence of the child upon the nape of its neck with its shoulders spread out, and its face turned towards its mother's back." "It is necessary for the midwife to have her hand on the child's head and also turn it little by little, and bring it out with ease."
"And when that is done and when it has been scraped, then place upon its head what we have described of oil and mucilages."
"And then command her to rub it little by little, and when you have done that, then make her sit upon a cushion and command her to lean towards the right side, and also command her to press herself, and make her sneeze with incense." "Emergence of the prepared fetus upon one side."
"When there is horrible emission from the mother according to this manner, consider it, and then make an incision with your nail into the second one until it is evacuated of moisture."
"And if the child is suspended upon its face and nape of the neck, then make an incision into the belly to prevent it from being retained and dying."
"And then push the child towards its parts inside until you place it according to what is necessary, and command the woman to press herself several times, and it will be forgotten with light emergence if God wills it."
"Emergence of twins or multiple fetuses." "Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four, but this is rare and strange, though it happens by nature's decree."
"And count those [ovaries], whether they be multiplied or not, and separate them by cyphac, distinguish each one within the ligament in the navel of each."
"And if some of them are difficult to remove at childbirth and arrive at what we have said about the unnatural shapes, then you take care of those as we have recounted."
"And if the midwife is subtle and does what she does with ease and subtlety, and slowly, and has the skill according to all shapes as it was prepared by the ingenious [person] bringing about health."
"Remembrance of that which is formed in the womb from embryos and those which are aborted."
"Some are formed in the mother's womb one by one, two by two, three by three, four by four, five by five, six by six, seven by seven, and more than ten, and it has been verified that one woman aborted six, and another gave birth to all ten, fully formed, which is a cause noted by the glorious wise men through measurement."
"And also, it belongs to the science of the midwife to know well that which is similar in this small creature, and therefore she should pause at that until she knows what it is."
"Chapter seventy-six."
"About removing the fetus when it is dead."
When you treat a dead fetus according to what we have said in the section on medicine and it has not yet emerged, and you wish to use manual operation, then consider if the woman is of sound virtue and not among those with conditions which could lead to harm upon her.
Then the woman should be placed on her left side on the bed, with her head lowered and her hips elevated.
And the assistant should hold her from both sides or tie her to the bed so that her body does not extend during the extraction of the fetus.
And then you moisten the mother's mouth with humid oil and a poultice made from marshmallow, fenugreek, and sesame seeds.
And then the midwife anoints her hand with those oils and poultices, and gently inserts it into the mother's mouth, and seeks with her hand the place where the hooks will be inserted in the fetus.
And the appropriate places for this are: then consider if the fetus is prepared to be expelled from its head and position the hooks accordingly in one of these locations: its cheeks, its neck, its mouth, its palate, below its chin, at its beard, at its collarbone, near its ribs, or below its chest.
But if the expulsion is happening from the feet of the fetus, then place the hooks on its heels or on the middle of its back.
And hold the hook with your right hand and pause its curvature in that place between the fingers of your left hand. Then gently insert your hand into the appropriate location we mentioned earlier until you reach the cause of the obstruction.
"And then place one or two additional pillows near them to support their back, ensuring they lie evenly and do not extend beyond their usual position."
"And also heat should be applied to the entire area, so that the inflammation is relieved as it would be during the eradication of the tooth."
"And also ensure that the extension is softened with water; and if any part of it is retained, then the midwife should anoint some of her fingers with oil and carefully insert them and move them about with the water that is retained."
"Therefore if the childbirth is delayed, then let the hands be changed for another who can be more useful; and do this until the entire childbirth has been completed."
"But if the hand becomes stuck before the other one, and it is not possible to reduce that by pressing on it, then a cloth should be wrapped around that; and carefully pull that out until everything has been delivered, and incise either at the joint of the hand or in the elbow."
"And likewise do this with the other hand and with both feet."
"But if the head of the child is large or there is difficulty in its delivery due to contraction of the passage, or it is stuck at the entrance of the waters, then let the space between the aforementioned spinous processes be opened and cut the head and remove the water, or else use an instrument called "alundat" to perform this operation, the form of which will come with the forms of other instruments in the chapter that follows."
"And similarly do this if the child has a large head by nature: and then it is necessary to incise with an instrument called "gemat", or use the aforementioned "alundat" in this way as we have said; and afterwards remove the bones with forceps."
"And if the head has exited but is constricted behind the pubic arch, then let it be cut until the humidity that is in the pelvis has flowed out."
"But if there are no complications and the birth is not obstructed, then you should incise the head as soon as it is possible for you."
"And if the left side of the belly is inflamed or in a state of dropsy, then it is necessary for you to pierce it until the humor that is inside it flows out."
"But if the child is above its own feet, then its attraction will be light and its direction towards the mouth of the mother will be easy."
"But if it is constricted behind the belly and the pelvis, then you should remove it with cloth that you will have wrapped around your hand, and cut the belly and pelvis until water flows from them."
"But if the other members are obstetrical and the head returns, then let the metron enter with the left hand; but if the mother's mouth is covered, then let the hand enter into the perineum of the vulva, grasp the head with it, draw it with the aforementioned entrance to the mother's mouth, and afterwards insert one or two hooks and draw it with those."
"And if the mother's mouth is obstructed by an ulcerative swelling that has occurred on her lip, then it should not be troubled with that; but at that time it is necessary to administer a purge of thick humid causes." "And apply poultices; and follow the patient with waters that soften and moisturize."
"And if the child is lying on its side, then if it is possible, turn it; and administer what we have said for a live birth."
"But if that is not possible, then let it be incised in pieces, and let it be removed."
"And you must not leave any cause inside the secondine."
"And when you have completed your entire operation, then administer what we have said about the cure of ulcerative swellings that occur in the mother."
"And if there occurs a flow of blood, then let her drink waters that are styptic and administer the other cure."
"And I have seen a woman in whose belly there was a dead child, and again afterwards pregnant over that same focus, and again the child was dead." "It happened to him that for a long time an ulcerative swelling appeared on his abdomen; and it swelled until the focus was covered, and he began to have pain in his arm."
"And I was called to cure him, and I treated him for a long time, but the plague did not consolidate."
"Then I applied over it poultices of strong attraction for some causes, and removed from him one bone, and after some days passed, I removed another bone. And I was very amazed, because there are no bones in the belly."
"And then I realized that they were the bones of the dead child."
"Therefore I cured the ulcerative swelling, removed from him many bones, the woman existed in good health, and already lived for a long time, running around without any pain in her arm."
"And I do not affirm that this is strange, but rather because in this there is science and help for the artisan physician who administers cure with his hand."

"On the extraction of the afterbirth."
"When the afterbirth is retained during childbirth, then you must command the midwife to retain her breath, and then make the woman sneeze with some condition, and stretch your hand over its mouth and nostrils, and if it comes out by this means, that's good."
"And if not, then you take a cloth and make a hole in it and place it over the mouth of the womb with these herbs burned: calamint, rue, fennel, camomile, saffron, and costus." "All these herbs or some of them are submerged in water in the cloth, and place it over the fire."
"And then place a reed cane in the mouth of the womb, and keep it there until the vapor comes to the cavity of the womb."
"And then make her sneeze as we have said, and the afterbirth will come out quickly expelled."

And when she has found it, then take it out little by little. But if it is attached to the lining of the womb, then insert your hand as we have recommended, and when you have found the afterbirth, extract it gradually according to rightness so that the woman does not suffer from violent traction." "It is necessary that they be changed on the right and left sides with ease."
