"And keep that up until that fumigation is consumed and repeat another."
"On the treatment of the unperforated anus in childbirth."
"Many newborns have unperforated anuses which are very thin and closed." "So the midwife must perforate that with her finger; if not, then perforate it with a sharp probe, taking care not to touch the nerve."
"And then place lanolin soaked in wine and oil over it; and dress it with ointment until healed."
"But if you fear that it may close again, then place a probe cannula in the hole for several days and remove it when the child wants to defecate."
"And sometimes the anus closes due to consolidation of a phlegm or an abscess; then that consolidation should be incised and then dressed with what we have said about the treatment and lead."
"On the treatment of fistulas that form in the rectum."
"The fistulas that develop in the lower part of the rectum are large and thick, which develop near the anus outside or in the space between the two buttocks."
"And it is one fistula or many."
"And with that thickness being old and running with moist white humidity or subtle pus, and sometimes there are penetrating parts from these fistulas."
"And these penetrating parts are recognized by what comes out of them through their exit and windiness; and sometimes the disease itself shows the exit, and sometimes it is clearly evident when worms come out."
"And sometimes there are penetrating parts from those fistulas entering the bladder and the glans of the penis; and these penetrating parts enter the junction of the vulva and into the opening of the vagina."
"And that which distinguishes a penetrating fistula from one that does not penetrate is this: when you insert your finger into the anus and find no tortuosity in the fistula, then it is not penetrating."
"If it is tortuosity in that area, then insert into that subtle vein of lead or horsehair until you feel the vein or hair under your finger."
"If you do not find anything at all and there is no evidence of obstruction, inflammation or wind, as mentioned earlier, then you should know that it is not penetrable, and therefore cease treatment."
"And when the fistula is penetrable into the bladder or into the urethra, its meaning is the escape of urine from there and the prevention of it, as this location is well-established in medicine."
"But if it is penetrable into the joint of the hip or into the bone and there is pain in the region, its sign is that the vein has entered here, unless it is tortuosity within the bone, causing pain at the outset. And from this, it always results in gangrene; and no remedy helps there, nor is it established with ointment."
"And in all those penetrable fistulas there is no cure at all, and the treatment of them is the fruitless labour and folly of foolish physicians."
"But in that which is not penetrable and is not old, healing with iron is hoped for according to what you will advise, based on what I have already said."
"And it is that the disease passes between your thighs and mostly on the two sides, raising its swellings within them. The hips are inclined towards the belly of it, and it enters with a tendency to plumb or earth if there is tortuosity in the fistula, so you should know the place where the vein has entered."
"And if that one feels the disease around his buttocks, then it is necessary for you to insert your little finger into the anus."
"And if you feel the vein already entering uncovered with your little finger, unless you feel something between the little finger and that flesh or skin, then you should know for certain that it is penetrable; and therefore do not treat that one, because there is no cure for him, as we have said."
"But nevertheless some say that some men are cured."
"And of the treatment by which it is hoped to obtain benefit from it, it is that you ignite cautery subtly according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before, and insert that burning into the fistula until it reaches around the anus; and then repeat that two or three times until you know that all those flesh joined by the fistula are burnt, which resemble the quill of a bird's feather."
"And then dress that with compresses wrapped in bandages until all those burnt flesh have cooled down, and also treat it with medicines that generate and solidify the flesh. And if it is healed, well and good; but if not, then it will never be healed by any other treatment."
"And if the vein enters but does not penetrate within the little finger which is in the anus, and between that and the vein which is veiled by skin or flesh, and sometimes the fistula runs along the surface of the thigh, then cut off the thigh from the beginning of the fistula. And you see it being cut with the vein, until the section reaches the place where the extremity of the vein has entered. And through the vein it will be freed and cured."
"And then cleanse those flesh joined by the fistula which resemble a bird's feather quill, and do not break them off for any reason."
"But if there is a flow of blood which comes between you and your operation when you are cutting those flesh, then the best thing to do is cauterize with fire or with an acute medicine, because cautery with fire has two good habits: it is the burning of those joined flesh, and the ablation of blood, exsiccation of humidity."
"And then dress it with compresses wrapped in bandages or in clean cloth until that place becomes sound. And then afterwards treat the wound with hard and solidifying medicine."
"And such medicines are those which have astringent and drying properties; when they are applied, the wound is restored and it will never be inflamed again."
"But if the fistula has already entered into the anus and is elongated along the surface of the body, then insert your little finger into the anus and search with it."
"And therefore if you feel the vein and between it and yourself there is veiled skin or flesh which prevents penetration, then it is not an operation but according to faith and hope."
"And therefore in this case there are three ways to proceed: either cauterize it as we have said; or dry it out until you achieve the concavity of it so that you can insert your finger into it and perform the proposed cure. And do not proceed with cutting because you might wound the lappet containing the anus, which would cause great suffering for the patient without his consent. And then dress it as we have said because it will heal quickly. Or else elongate that veil and clean out the pus from there near the anus as we have said, either with your finger or with another instrument of pointed extremity. And then cleanse those flesh joined by the fistula which are in the section where you can perform cauterization. And finally strive to make the restoration of all the wound with a cut, and if the upper opening is not solidified, and the fistula remains open at the partition of the anus, then it will cause further suffering." "And when the fistula is finished in this manner: it is when you insert your finger into the fistula, and on the side of the anus around the surface of the body with the thigh, then take a needle with a perforated extremity which is like the one used for preparing hearts in this form:"
"and insert it into that vein wrapped with a thread or around those veins, and then insert your finger with the thread into the fistula until you achieve the concavity of it."
"But if it is penetrating into the margin of the anus deeply, then you pull out the thread from that wound in such a way that you insert your little finger into the anus. And then extract the extremity of the thread and join both extremities together. Then cut each one separately, and leave it like that for one day or two days. And when you see that the thread has become incorporated into the flesh, then cut it carefully until those flesh which are between both extremities of the thread have fallen off."
"And then dress the wound until it is solidified and healed."
"But if the opening of the fistula is not penetrating, then make it penetrate, in whatever way you are prepared to do so, but not too deeply into the anus because you should not do this yourself lest you wound the lappet. And then dress it until it is healed."
"The form of the spatula with spines used to open the fistula is like this: its curvature is very sharp and the other edge is not sharp so that you do not wound anything unnecessarily, as it happens often."
"On the suture of hemorrhoids which bleed at the incision of those."
"There are two kinds of hemorrhoids: one is between the buttocks resembling these coals; the other is when those are like grapes." "And of those there are small and large ones; some always bleed and are one; others are many and are outside the anus at its extremities."
"But those which are outside the anus are due to little humidity, from which yellow water or a little blood with continuous discharge comes out and they appear according to the color of the body."
"The cure for this condition, which affects the heart, is to order the patient to sit up and press their chest until the heart appears." "Then you will take hold of one with your fingers or whatever you have at hand, and carefully cut where their roots are."
"However, if your fingers are not strong enough because of the humidity and softening of those parts, then you should take them with rough cloth or cotton or a piece of woolen flannel, extract them with your hands, and carefully cut where their roots are. Then sprinkle some dry powder on that incision so that it may burn those parts instead of cauterizing." "And then treat those parts with the other cure until they are healed."
"And if the wound does not close, then you should cleanse the patient with a cleansing agent that causes a small bite. Let it be washed with water from the heart until it closes gently when the patient squeezes."
"But if the hemorrhoids are outside of the anus, then their cause is slight, and it is sufficient for you to take them with your fingernail or grasp them with a small forceps and cut them. Then treat them with water as previously mentioned until they are healed."
"And for one who has had an incision made beforehand, you should administer suturing of them in this manner: Take some linen thread and wrap it around a needle. Then insert the needle into the skin at the edges above where the hemorrhoids are located. Next, make the needle penetrate into the other part of the skin at the edge below. Wrap the two ends of the linen thread around the needle in such a way that they cross each other laterally. Then tie the hemorrhoid with great tension and cut off the excess linen thread."
"And do this for all of them, leaving one alone and not tying it, so that the superfluous blood may flow out from there."
"And then apply a cloth soaked in rose oil or wax over the anus, and also apply some on the belly. Command the patient to keep quiet." "And then leave that alone until it heals. And when it has healed, treat it with an ointment or another cure so that it may be healed."
"And if those are old and not useful in that medicine, then you must remove them with the point of a spatula or your fingernail until they are wet and remove the pus on top, which prevents consolidation; and then cure them once they have consolidated."
"Then remove those with violent scraping until the first blood comes out and they are raw; then cure them once they are healed."
"Know that leprosy, the key disease, is not recognizable by any reddening of the skin like a pinhead; rather it appears throughout the body but most notably on the sides of the feet and hands, where pain often occurs."
"And then it is necessary that this be inscribed on what is in the circuit of the key and held with forceps or tweezers and removed from its root; then cure it."
"And if you wish, cauterize the second one that preceded it on its head."
"However, a wart is a small, rough, flesh-colored elevation with a round, indented surface that appears most often on the faces of children."
"And its treatment is to stretch and incise it, or scrape it off with a file or pumice stone until it bleeds." "If you wish, cauterize it with fire or an acute medicine, as we have said."
"However, a mole is a small, fatty or flesh-colored elevation with a rough surface that appears frequently on the forehead. When it is rubbed with a finger, it resembles the bite of an ant; they are found all over the body."
"And its treatment is to take a quill of an owl or vulture feather, thick and sharp, place it on the mole so that the circle of the quill contains the mole's perimeter; then rotate your hand with the quill so as to incise what is around the mole, pressing down on the skin. Then eradicate the mole from its root."
"And if you wish, do it with a cautery iron or red-hot needle in this way:"
"Make the tip of the needle thin, blunt (i.e., not perforated), and covered with something so that when you hold it, its point is smooth and easy to rotate."
"And if you wish, cauterize the mole according to what was said earlier in the chapter on cautery regarding the treatment of warts."
"On the shapes of the instruments used for cautery."
"Sometimes cautery is performed using silver or lead or molten iron or brass; and sometimes it is done with small or large instruments according to what is available. For example, the instrument used for treating young children should be small. And those whose handles are crooked or bent, their cauteries should also be small."
"The shape of a large cautery with few points:"
"The head of the cautery needle at its top should be wide like this; and it should have the same distance from where the purse is tied to where it ends."
"And the bottom end of it that is inserted into the handle should be blunt (i.e., not open) but pointed at its tip, tapering to a sharpness. And on one side there should be two holes and on the other side one hole, with the width of the holes being according to the thickness of the rays, with larger ones being smaller."
"And the purse in which bladder medicines from beasts or sheep wool are placed should have a root of one palm [approximately 7.62 cm]."
"And it should be pierced with many holes around it, so that when it is rotated, the space between the holes is equal to the thickness of your finger."
"And then insert strong, hot iron wire through the holes of the purse. After inserting it, fit the purse onto the cautery instrument and tighten it securely at the top of the cautery between two points with great force. Then cauterize using this method for each hole: But the key to cauterizing in this way is that you should fill the purse with the medicine, heated according to the tolerance level of the patient; be careful not to make it too hot or too cold."
"And then have the patient lie on their back and raise their buttocks up. Place a cloth or towel underneath them to protect them from soiling themselves. Then apply oil or egg white or fenugreek mucilage or similar substance to the tip of the cautery instrument, insert it into the anus gently, then have the assistant take the purse, squeeze it with both hands and press it vigorously until everything inside the cautery is expelled from the bowel. Then remove the cautery instrument and let the patient lower their buttocks back down."
"If the medicine forces them to evacuate strongly, have them hold it as long as they can. And if they sleep with that in place for the whole night, it will be more effective in its action."
"But if you cauterize someone for disorders of the belly with evacuation and bleeding from there, then repeat the cautery procedure until they are healed."
"And if there are hemorrhoids or bleeding fistulas in the anus, then use a small and pointed cautery, such as those used for cauterizing children."
"On treating plagues:"
"I have already mentioned in the division of plague treatments what was necessary for this book. And I will now explain how to treat them using me and medicines according to their respective requirements."
"So I say that plagues are differentiated according to the condition in which they occur, and according to the location where the plague occurs."
"And the causes why plague often occurs are as follows: such as fracture of bone, or incision with knife or spear, or cut with sword, or blow with lance, club, or arrow, or similar things from many causes."
"But the plagues that occur in different parts of the body are as follows: such as plague that occurs on the head, neck, chest, abdomen, buttocks, and similar ones on the limbs."
"And I am recounting here the treatment of some plagues because this reasoning and rule can also apply to other plagues."
"I will begin with simple head wounds, as the treatment of compound ones will come at the beginning of the third chapter."
"So I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head and it is not a fracture, then consider this: if it was caused by a blow from a stone or similar object and only the scalp has been affected, and it is a large wound and you fear that there may be an abscess forming, then immediately perform a cephalic trepanation and flebotomy on the head. Do not delay in doing this, unless there is some other reason preventing flebotomy, especially if the blood that has flowed from the wound is sparse."
"And perform the trepanation on the opposite side of the parted wound. Keep the patient from exertion and strong drink, as well as heavy food."
"But if you prohibit any cause because of the minuteness of it, then let him have only light food and avoid meat and wine."
"And pause on the wound. If an abscess forms, cut into it with roasted rose oil or wine mixed with tragacanth gum."
"If you are certain of an abscess, then place hot water over the inflammation if it is recent, mixed with its blood and air has not changed that powder which I will recommend soon."
"If the air has already changed there, then place hot water over the ulcer until it is healed."
"If the wound is large or made by a sword cut and does not have its edges aligned due to dust, then align them with stitches according to my recommendation for wound stitching."
"If the wound is already open and exposed to the bone and only has slight swelling rather than retention, then incision should be made there and appropriate care given to the wound using medicines. The flesh should also be restored appropriately in place of sutures, and the patient commanded to abstain from foods that are coarse: cabbage, beans, peas, lentils and similar things, until recovery is complete."
"If you find putrefaction in the wound and it does not adhere to the bone, then incise all that is putrid, remove it, and dress the wound appropriately."
"If in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which blood flows profusely and cannot be stopped by medicines, then inquire about the artery. If you find that it has not been incised, then incise it with a scalpel or ligate it; if necessary, cauterize until the bleeding stops."
"If these wounds are simple and small, then their cause is light. Therefore, you should powder them with this powder, so that they may be consolidated before the air can change them."
"And the method for making this powder is as follows: take one part oil of sesame, two parts dragon's blood resin, three parts myrrh resin; grind them all together and sift it. Use this powder to fill the wound and constrain it with good constriction until it adheres well and coagulates with the blood."
"And then apply this powder to it from above and leave it alone. Do not remove it while it is still adhering, because the medicine has not yet been eradicated from there until it is healed."
"Sometimes you can use only cauterization when sesame oil and dragon's blood resin are not available to you."
"And this same operation should be performed on large wounds when it is appropriate to place them over those and they are straitened, especially fresh wounds with their blood, which have not yet been altered by the air."
"But if the air has altered them, especially during summer time, then it is not appropriate to use this powder. In that case, treat those wounds with what we have said earlier: apply some suitable ointments over them, or use flour of barley mixed with water and honey until they become putrid; and then treat them with the other cure until they are healed."
"But if a fracture of the bone occurs in a wound that is small, then you should treat it with this [powder]."
"And I say that the treatment for fractures of the head is given above."
"Regarding wounds of the neck:"
"But if a wound occurs on the neck, there is no difference in treatment between it and a simple head wound."
"But if the nerve or artery of the neck is cut, then if it is a nerve, there is no other means than to avoid treatment with this [powder] that causes violent coagulation, such as vitriol and similar substances which harm nerves." "And do not apply any cautery to the wound for any reason, because the substance of nerves is fragile and their continuity is with the brain, which is the master of all members."
"And if it is treated with light medicines in this way, such as washing the wound with warm water, sometimes infused in uncooked or cooked oil, and then applying honey when washed with warm water and other minor ointments according to this method, and moistening them."
"But if the wound is large, then perform suturing or fasten the lips of it, and afterwards treat it with this powder until it is healed."
"But if the wound has depth or if it occurs in a low-lying part that becomes putrid, then pierce it at its deepest point."
"But if an artery is cut in the wound and bleeding occurs, then separate or dry it out, ligate it, or cauterize it if necessary."
"But if the vertebrae of the spine have been severed completely and the veins of the neck are preserved, then approximate the lips of the wound over the spine with suturing without touching that part. Then elevate it gently and reduce it to its natural shape. Afterwards strengthen it with decent traction, leave it alone for a few days; and afterwards treat it with ointments that have coagulating and stimulating properties until it is healed."
"But if the wound has already reached the bone, then strike it with a mallet. And if there are fragments of bone in it, remove all that you can. But what cannot be removed, leave it alone until the wound becomes putrid and separates, and its inflammation is relieved."
"And if the wound is fresh, then powder it with the powder that I have recommended to you." "But if there is a fistula in the wound, then treat it with what will be remembered shortly in its proper chapter."
"If it is a wound made by a lance or knife, and its depth varies according to the force of the blow, then consider whether there is any wind sound coming from the wound when the patient breathes. If so, know that the wound is mortal."
"And if it is not deep and the wound is fresh with its own blood, then pause in it with the first-hour powder, but do not compress it so that the blood does not accumulate in its depth and return to the heart causing harm. Instead, apply an attractive ointment and wash it twice a day."
"And if the ointment is not available, then place a piece of cotton in the wound to prevent anything from flowing out, and make sure that the patient sleeps on their side so that what has accumulated flows out."
"But if three days or more have passed and no spasm, heart palpitations, or lung constriction has occurred in the patient, and other conditions are good, then know that the wound is safe. And so treat it with bandages and other treatments until it is healed."
"But if its healing is delayed and much time has passed, then know that a fistula has already formed. Therefore treat it according to the chapter on fistulas."
"And if the wound is caused by a cut from a sword or knife and is simple on the surface of the skin or flesh, then treat it with what has been previously mentioned about suturing if it is large, or with powder if it is small."
"But if the wound has already reached the bone and pieces of it have been cut off, then turn the wound over and try to extract those pieces if they are separate." "But if they are not separate, then leave them alone until the wound becomes putrid, for their extraction will be easier that way."
"And regarding other accidental wounds in the other members, the remedy in treatment is the same as what has been said."
"Regarding abdominal wounds:"
"The condition that occurs in the abdomen is either large, small, or medium-sized."
"When extraction is requested, it is difficult to achieve by other methods, and especially if the reduction of these is more difficult, unless you quickly remove the intrusion from its place, for if it opens and becomes enlarged because the entrance was difficult."
"The best extraction is through the middle, for in that case it is easy to reduce the intestines, unlike in the two species mentioned above."
"And you should know that there are four ways to suture the abdomen, but two of these sutures are common and applicable to other wounds on the body."
"And the other two sutures are more specific to the abdomen, although they can be applied to other wounds as well."
"I will now recount each one with its exposition and explanation."
"Therefore I say that when the wound is small and some cause of the intestines comes out through it, and it is difficult to reduce it, there are two ways: either because of the smallness of the disruption, as we have said, or when inflammation has come to the intestines due to the coldness of the air."
"And therefore, when this is the case, you should then scrape that until you immerse a sponge or cloth wet in hot water alone, or you take water with squinant, cyperus, and spice, and bandage it around that part of the intestines so that the inflammation may be resolved."
"And sometimes you will find this useful in cases where there is stricturing, and it is better that the water alone be used for resolving the inflammation."
"Therefore, once the inflammation has been resolved, you should then moisten the intestines with water in which common salt and mallows have been boiled, for this relieves the pain caused by it."
"But if the pain has not been relieved by this treatment, then carefully cut the disruption a little with an instrument with which it is incised, and remove theemorrhoids."
"And the primary treatment is better, when it is proper that it not be cut, and there is no need to cut except in case of necessity or deficiency."
"What is the shape of the instrument?"
"The one end of it is cut sharp, and the other not sharp, and the tip is subtle, but not as subtle as a spatula, rather it is somewhat obtuse."
"And therefore, once the wound has been enlarged and extends outside the intestines, it is necessary that its reduction be according to the shape of nature itself in its proper place, if this is possible. For this is better."
"But when the disruption is large and it is in the lower part of the belly, then you should make the sick person lie on his back, raise his buttocks as high as his head; but if it is in the upper part of the belly, then you should raise his head and raise his feet as high as the sides."
"And likewise if the disruption is in one of the two sides of the belly, then always pay attention and consideration to this, so that the side where there is the wound may be raised higher than the other."
"And this you should administer in both large wounds and medium-sized ones."
"And in small wounds, pay attention to what you have prepared, and especially that the person who ministers it be among your most skilled, who should hold the disruption entirely with his hand and adjust its lips together, and so that he may cover from this one to that which sews without any other cause."
"And this is the common manner of suturing: first take the needle, or count of needles according to the amount of the width of the wound; and then leave the end of the disruption on the finger, and thread the needle once, but do not put silk in both ends of the thread. With two ends of the silk, which is left outside the thread, enter it into that part until you have brought it out from there; and you already have four orders."
"And then thread with doubled silk around the needle, and sometimes from two parts together, and then join the two lips and the wound by proper joining; and then leave the thickness of the finger and insert another needle into it, and then tie that with silk in the same way as the first needle was tied. And do not cease doing this until you have completed all the contraction of the wound."
"And let the needles be medium between thickness and subtlety, for the thin needles easily cut into the flesh; but thick ones are difficult to insert into the thread. Therefore they should be medium in subtlety and thickness."
"And it is not necessary that the needle be inserted into both ends of the thread very close together, for fear that the flesh should be easily cut and that the wound may open before its consolidation."
"And do not make sutures too long so that the wound is not prevented from consolidation."
"And then cut the ends of the needles so that they do not bother the sick person while he is sleeping. And you will put powdered incense on the sutures from both sides, which should hold the ends of the needles; and leave them there until you know that the wound has already consolidated."
"And these kinds of sutures with needles in whatever manner are more convenient for small wounds, since it is enough to use one needle or two or around them."
"But the second suture is more common: and it is that you administer with sutures the four ends of the thread and both ends of the silk in one time, with a needle on which there is silk wrapped in subtlety and thickness."
"And then when the needle has penetrated these four ends, reduce the needle from that same part where you began, so that the silk may draw back from the uppermost part of the wound to the bottom, so that the suture may be like a seam on cloth with which the threads are tightened."
"And put between each suture the quantity of the thickness of the little finger."
"And this is what people know."
"And with this suture I sewed a wound which had been accidentally inflicted on a man in his belly, who had been wounded with a dagger, and the disruption of the wound was more than a palm; it had exited from the intestines around two palms from the middle of the intestine, and the disruption was in the middle of the member. And then I reduced that after the intestines had been forced out by the wound for twenty-four hours."
"And the wound was consolidated in the space of fifteen days or thereabouts, and he was cured. And he lived for many years after that, and is still alive in his usual condition."
"And the other doctors had judged that he would not be healed. And by miracle it was so, for I did not cure him with an ointment, because there was no ointment nor any medicine to be found in that place; but twice a day I put a cloth moistened with honey water on the wound until he was healed."
"But I say two kinds of sutures proper according to the narration of the Word."
"And it is that you begin with suturing the thread and insert the needle from without into within."
"And then when the needle penetrates into the thread and in that same part of the flesh according to its breadth and length throughout all the body, leave the end of the silk on which you have inserted the needle; and make the needle penetrate from within outwards in the other extremity of the member."
When you have caused it to penetrate once, then cause it to penetrate again in that same spot of the right side outside to inside; and leave the extremity of the spleen which is on this side, and cause the needle to penetrate into the other extremity of the inside from the outside.
And cause that penetration with which you cause it to penetrate in the spleen at the extremity of the mirror which is inside that everything may penetrate.
And start from this same side and count with the extremity which is of the spleen on the other side, and withdraw the needle from the channel which you have penetrated, and again insert it into that channel and pass through the extremity of the spleen which is on the other side with this extremity of the mirror; and withdraw it from the channel which is towards them.
And do this once or twice, and do this once again if you wish to do everything that is outside according to that example.
And the sum of this manner of suturing is that you should suture with a suturing of the skin in such a way that you should suture the spleen once from the side of the channel extremity, and leave the other side until it has been completed.
Moreover, the second species of suturing which Guilia describes explicitly, and this is about it and for its recommendation, is that you should suture it according to semilunar fashion with which some surgeons suture it, so that they join every part to its corresponding part according to nature; and they apply the extremity of one side and the extremity of the mirror to the other extremity of it, and this is done as you recommend.
Certainly you should leave the needle in the extremity of the mirror at your proximity to the outside part, and make it penetrate into the inside part in that same sun, and leave both extremities of the spleen; and again turn the needle and make it penetrate from outside to inside through both extremities of the spleen.
And again turn those shuttles, and make them penetrate from the inside part into the outside part through both extremities of the mirror except those which are on the opposite side.
And this manner of suturing is better than the common light suturing, and it is the suturing of which a preceding mention has been made.
This is the speech of Guilia
And some say that abdominal suturing is corrected with two needles, so that you should put in these shuttles a filet, and begin with the needle insertion of what is required by you, and make it penetrate into the other side according to the suturing of those who suture the hearts equally.

But the treatment of a wound is judged by other wounds.
"The cause is that when you constrain the wound recently with its own blood before the air alters it, and reduce the intestine, close it, and prepare it properly, then place powdered cinnabar on it."
"If the air has already altered the wound, then place this powder on it with great care using these cloths that are nearby to make sure it penetrates deep and sticks well."
"But if you are not present, then apply the powder immediately, because it begins to heal within three days and changes every two days, as you have taught, until it is healed. For you do not need other medications in many cases when wounds are simple."
"But if you fear that the wound may communicate with injury to the principal members, then you should submerge lion's wool in good quality olive oil or rose oil and apply it to the area between the joints and leave it on."
"And if there is pain or putrefaction in its bowels, which often happens, then crystallize this with black treacle wine and more so if the putrefaction has reached the bowel and cannot be expelled."
"And know that a wound in the large intestine is of lighter healing than one in the small intestines."
"And it is difficult to heal because the intestine called 'gegunu' does not receive healing of any wound that falls into it; and this is due to the great multitude of veins that are in it and the magnitude of its substance, and for the subtlety of its body and its proximity to the nature of nerves."
"But if what proceeds from the wound is tissue and you obtain that recent, then reduce it according to your discretion with which you also reduce intestines equally."
"But if it has passed into blackness and is becoming green or black, then strengthen it with faith over the area that has been discolored by it, so that fluxes of blood may come forth, for in the tissue are veins and arteries."

"Remembrance of wounds when they occur in the intestine."
"When disruption occurs in the intestine and it is small, then it is possible that it may be restored in some people, for this reason: one man who was wounded in his belly with a lance blow and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and the wound was old and had no fistula, and from it there was management and windiness."
"Then I followed the treatment of it although it was not certain in its healing, but I ceased to subtiliate that which was inside it and the area had consolidated."
"And I put that I saw the area already consolidated, so I placed on him a remedy for the pain that occurred over his belly wound; and no one else suffered from this accident, and they remained in their best condition eating and drinking, and appropriately entered into baths and were exercised in their deeds."
"And some experienced ones have said that when there is wound in the intestine and it is small, then it is necessary to ligate it in this manner: And take figs with large heads; and appropriately adjust both lips of the wound and place one of those which has its mouth open over both lips of the wound. Then when it adheres there and tightens its mouth, cut off its head for it adheres and is not dissolved."
"And appropriately place another fig near the first one, and do not cease doing this with figs until the quantity of the entire wound is filled."
"And appropriately reduce it and sew the wound shut; and those attached heads remain inside the intestine until the intestine is healed; and no one suffers from any harm."

"And this manner of suturing with figs is nothing but a way of trust and hope."

"On the treatment of tumor and fistula."
"You should know that every wound and abscess when it becomes hollowed out and ancient, and is made into an ulcer, and does not consolidate and emits branch always without being cut off, then universally it is named fistula, and we call it that tumor."
"And truly, fistula is a hard, white, tough node without pain with which there is concavity just as there is concavity of the navel; and for this reason it is called that ulcerous boil, that is to say navel."
"And in some people it is humid, which emits branch; and sometimes the humidity is cut off in a few hours." "Sometimes this humidity is much, little, thick, and subtle."
"I have already shown all those causes and the signs of them and their cure with medicines in the division."
"And it is necessary that I make you know the treatment of fistula which is done by means of operation with a knife."
"And you should know that fistula occurs in all the members of the body; for some of them pertain to the great veins and arteries, or to the nerves, or to the bladder, or to the intestine, or to the urinary bladder, or to one of the ribs, or to some of the vertebrae of the back, or to one of the joints composed by composition such as those of the hand and foot; and some of them have relation to the principal member and similar ones."
"And therefore those of these fistulas that are in this manner are among the illnesses of difficult healing and they do not receive cure and care with them is work and ignorance."
"And if there is any fistula whose depth does not reach those places that I have mentioned and you hope for its cure but you want to know about it, then take a thread of wool or iron, and if the fistula goes straight, examine it with it."
"If the fistula is twisted, then examine it with a thin lead probe, for lead has the lightness of its body and curves towards the twist."
"And if the fistula is without any movement or horror, you will not be able to designate anything by means of it."
"Then crystallize the horrifics for their own sake, because the moisture with which you crystalize them will flow towards the other horrifics and run from them."

"And therefore if it is healed, good. But if not, then know that that corruption is in the distant depth of the body, which has not been reached, and therefore in that case there is nothing else to do but leave it alone."
"And if the corrupted bone is small or can be removed by you, then remove it with subtle forceps which are suitable for that."

Leave this in place until the flesh and membranes have grown around the bones, and keep the plug from becoming consolidated, and strengthen the section which you have incised during your operation."

"Of cutting off extremities and sawing bones."
"Extremities can be removed either due to an intrinsic cause or extrinsic cause, or when you have treated that corruption with curative medicines and the cure does not confer, sometimes the corruption goes into a member which does not persecute any cause; therefore it is necessary for you to cut off that member within which the corruption has occurred, because the illness will disappear through that of death or malice which is greater damage to the member."

The method of incising the member or severing it is that you stretch the ligament at the part where you want to cut, and then stretch another ligament above the location. The minister should extend one ligament on each side of the place to be cut, and the other minister should extend another ligament above them. Then you separate the flesh between the two ligaments with a wide-bladed knife until all the flesh is exposed. Then it can be incised or severed.
It is necessary to bind the limbs on all sides so that they do not touch the location where it will be operated on, and that the patient suffers only just injury and a clean wound.
But if bleeding occurs while operating, then cauterize the location carefully, or apply some powder made from dry red roses to stop the bleeding. Then return to your treatment until it is completed.
And then bind the member gently with a bandage in whatever way seems convenient, and take care of it until it is healed.
And I advise you that once happened to a man on his foot, this accident which you and I are discussing, which is that it occurred due to the blackness of the skin on his foot caused by burning similar to fire combustion.
And that corruption first began in his toe and then spread throughout the entire foot.
Then that man prepared himself to apply pus every day since the treatment had not been effective in relieving the pain and burning sensation of the member. He incised the foot at its joint, and it healed with fire cauterization.
It has happened for a long time that that corruption comes into the tip of the finger.
And then it came to me, and I realized that that excess water had gathered on the hand with which I handled medications, precisely during the cleansing of the patient's body. And the excess water did not recede, but began to flow into another finger starting from the hand.
And he asked me to lance his hand, but I did not want to do so hoping that the excess water would recede. Indeed, I feared for the incision of his hand because the disease's strength was too great.
And after he parted from me, he returned to his land and it came to my knowledge that that man prepared himself and incised his own hand entirely, and was healed.
And I do not tell you this story except to aid those who may be afflicted with this disease, and that there may be meaning in it for the one to whom it is told and according to which it should be acted upon.
De cura sinusum et qualitate clisterizationis cum medicinis.
When an aposteme occurs on some fleshy member and the space of the aposteme is prolonged until it makes collection of pus, and then it breaks and perforates, and the pus comes out from it, and the place remains empty as if it were a vessel, and the cord that is over it appears thus like a subtly woven cloth, and there has not been any later corruption, and it does not impress on the bone or on nerve nor on ligament, it is called sinus, and it is not called fistula.
But if the space is prolonged until corruption impresses on some member, then it is called fistula and not sinus.
And the cure for it is to incise that cord entirely as it appears, and more so when it is thin like cloth, and you make sure that it does not adhere to the place by its corruption.
But if you wait for the cord to adhere and that corruption has not yet had its final course, and there has appeared a passage in the cord, then you treat it with a clyster.
And when you examine the sinus, if it is large and the arm that extends from it has a fetid odor, then you clysterize it with Egyptian medicine which is made of oil and sour wine and salt receipt in equal parts, ground fine and adjusted in a vessel, and cooked over the fire until the medicine becomes thick like honey.
And then you take from it the amount that is necessary and dissolve it with water and honey; and you clysterize with that the sinus, and strengthen the opening of it, and leave the medicine in it for the duration of two hours.
And then you extract that with a probe; and do this for so many days until the sinus is cleaned out and the pus is removed.
And sometimes it is clysterized with water of ash when this medicine is not present; and you take the ashes of oak wood, put them on the water, then boil them and clysterize that with it until you are sure that the sinus has been cleaned out.
And if the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine nor the water of ash, then you clysterize it with water and honey mixed together three times, and you also clysterize it with wine and honey mixed together, because honey has the property to cleanse and wash, and wine makes the sinus adhere more, especially when there is an excess of astringency and dryness in the wine.
And when you do this several times and you are sure that the sinus has been removed, then you clysterize it with something that makes flesh grow in it.
And you take of the powder called diafinicon and dissolve it with rose oil and astringent wine, or you clysterize it with other medicines and ointments that have the properties which I have already written about in the treatise on ointments.
And if the opening of the sinus is narrow and cannot receive the cannula of the clyster, then you dilate it with a small iron probe little by little, and pause in it with cotton wrapped in Egyptian ointment or basilicon ointment until it has been dilated.
And similarly if the opening is wide, then you close its lips with a suture and leave in it the amount that intervenes between the clyster without adding anything else.
And if the opening of that from which the arm extends is elevated above the parts around it, then you close it with a bitumen plaster in such a way that the arm runs within it, because when the arm is tightened by the pressure of the sinus flesh will be generated in it.
And if you cannot close the sinus with bitumen plaster as you wish, then you make an incision into the member after preparing it in such a way that the arm runs out of it lightly according to what seems appropriate to you and without anything inside it that could impede the movement of the arm.
But that which is on the opening of the sinus should be removed immediately in order to remove whatever may have adhered to it from the arm. And so that you know if what comes out of it from the arm is much or little, whether it is digested or undigested.
And also consider the location of that sinus, whether the patient feels pain there or not, and if it is an abscess.
And when your treatment has lasted for a while in this manner and you see that the matter that is poured onto the opening of the sinus has already adhered or almost adhered, then on the third day remove it by tearing it off gently; and when you tear it off, then change the cloth for another one and renew the ointment.
But if from the sinus a long distance virus subtile issues forth, then do not despair of its adhesion, because the healing of it will occur, because there are some people in whom the generation of flesh is late in their wounds, and among those who the opposite occurs.
And if for many days an undigested arm comes out of the sinus, then you know that the sinus does not adhere; and if the adhesion of the sinus is delayed and the cause is prolonged, then you should apply dry medicines, and if the medicines are moist in their substance and virtue, they will be dry like diafinicon ointment when there is an excess of addition of egg yolk.
And the last remedy that remains is to take diafinicon ointment and dissolve it in rose oil, then add old wine to it in its substance, and apply it on top of it, and use it.
And do likewise in that action when there is no arm coming out of it: apply diafinicon ointment, honey when it has been cooked until thickened, and use it; or take myrrh and aloe and frankincense, grind everything and powder it over the honey while it is on the fire, then mix this onto a cloth and apply it on top of the sinus; and also apply that honey which you have cooked until thickened, powder it onto a cloth and apply it.
"Sometimes a long-armed plaster made of celestial lily (and it is called celestial lily) and ground barley and centaurea is administered."
"If the pain persists and is not healed by this treatment, you should know that the corruption is in the patient's throat. Then, make an investigation into the bones or other hard members or the ligaments."
"For the treatment of pimples and scratched nails, and for adding an extra digit and cutting it off."

It emits a dark red liquid that corrode the root of the nail, and sometimes it corrupts the whole of it, and sometimes its corruption reaches the bone, causing foul odor, and the tip of the finger turns black and its color becomes dark."
